### Review by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) (commented) — 2025-02-14T10:35:50Z

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:83** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:01:50Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
```

  fix formatting

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:152** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:02:14Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
+nominal quota, then it is admitted immediately, if not it goes into cohort-level fair sharing.
+For Cohort we select all the “sticking out” workloads, and sort them by their CQ usage, priority
```

  What is "sticking out"? I interpret it to mean `workload + previous usage > resources available without borrowing`. Could we define this?

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:57** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:04:11Z

```diff
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.

+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.

+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.

+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.

+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
```

  How will these mechanisms work together? Can we specify this in detail, or make these features mutually exclusive - only one of them may be enabled?
  
  I have a bias towards the latter approach, at the very least within the same (root)Cohort.

```diff
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
```

  fix formatting

```diff
+}

+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).

+

+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (

+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)

+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}

+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
```

  How do we indicate that these workloads are preemptible? Is this usage counted against this workload's fair sharing value?

```diff
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more.

+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues.

+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+

+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+

+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
```

  I would argue against supporting this mode. It seems complex, when the idea of this mode was to have fair sharing without preemption.
  
  Couldn't a user define some best-effort queue which sits outside of the admission scope, which may be preempted?

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:146** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:19:37Z

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)

+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more.

+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one

+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing

+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.

+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)

+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}

+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:

+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
+nominal quota, then it is admitted immediately, if not it goes into cohort-level fair sharing.
+For Cohort we select all the “sticking out” workloads, and sort them by their CQ usage, priority
+and timestamp. Kueue attempts to admit the first workload from the list of sticking-out, just
+like if it was one big strict FIFO queue. For multi-level hierarchy under one AdmissionScope
```

  What if the first workload fits from CQ, and after its admission the 2nd workload would require borrowing. Would we consider this 2nd workload at the Cohort level in the same scheduling cycle, or it is always one candidate per level per cycle? I suppose the second model is simpler, so I would favor it.

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:164** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:20:32Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)

+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources.

+

+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing

+

+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.

+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
+nominal quota, then it is admitted immediately, if not it goes into cohort-level fair sharing.
+For Cohort we select all the “sticking out” workloads, and sort them by their CQ usage, priority
+and timestamp. Kueue attempts to admit the first workload from the list of sticking-out, just
+like if it was one big strict FIFO queue. For multi-level hierarchy under one AdmissionScope
+we would treat underlying Cohorts as Fifo CQs.
+
+
+* Additionally there will be the resource usage calculation loop. The frequency of the
+calculation will be controlled globally in Kueue’s config file. Accounting would be done
+using something like geometric average:
+
+usage_sum = (1-A) * previous_usage_sum + A * current_usage.  
+
+The value will be stored in FairSharingStatus for all LQ, CQ, and Cohorts.
```

  This isn't only for information, but the working value we'll use upon Kueue restart? Does it belong in Status?

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:106** by [@gabesaba](https://github.com/gabesaba) — 2025-02-14T10:24:42Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
```

  Why? Let's make this invalid state, as the lower scope is doing nothing?

```diff
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing

+<!-- toc -->

+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+

+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
```

  > Inside CQ workloads are selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified)
  
  Only highest `AdmissionScope` is used. Do you mean Queueing Policy (FIFO/BestEffort)?

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:137** by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) — 2025-02-17T09:33:56Z

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)

+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
```

  ```suggestion
  Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is`UsageBasedFairSharing`), priority and
  ```

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
+nominal quota, then it is admitted immediately, if not it goes into cohort-level fair sharing.
+For Cohort we select all the “sticking out” workloads, and sort them by their CQ usage, priority
+and timestamp. Kueue attempts to admit the first workload from the list of sticking-out, just
+like if it was one big strict FIFO queue. For multi-level hierarchy under one AdmissionScope
+we would treat underlying Cohorts as Fifo CQs.
+
+
+* Additionally there will be the resource usage calculation loop. The frequency of the
+calculation will be controlled globally in Kueue’s config file. Accounting would be done
+using something like geometric average:
+
+usage_sum = (1-A) * previous_usage_sum + A * current_usage.  
+
+The value will be stored in FairSharingStatus for all LQ, CQ, and Cohorts.
+
+The user will be able to configure the decaying factor A in Kueue’s config file by specifying
+the half decay time - after what time the current shared usage will decay to half of its original value.
+
+A = 1 - 0.5 ^ (sampling/half_decay)
+
+* Configuration will sit in FairSharing stuct in Kueue config. There will be the following modifications:
+
+  - modes - decides which modes are enabled in FairSharing is turned on. By default it would be: [“PreemptionBased”]. Allowed values: “PreemptionBase”, “AdmissionTime”.
+  - usageHalfDecayTime - half decay time of usage, as described above.
+  - usageSamplingFrequency - how often usage is calculated.
+  - resourceWeights - how much consumption of individual resources is important when comparing usage.
```

  Could you expand on this? Are there any defaults for this?

```diff
+- Priority
```

  ```suggestion
  The usage vector will be sum of the `ConsumedResources` weighted according to `resourceWeights` (mentioned later in the KEP)
  ```

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:114** by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) — 2025-02-17T09:45:39Z

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)

+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+

+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
```

  Does it differ from excluding a CQ/Cohort from the new logic?

### Review by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) (commented) — 2025-02-21T12:11:18Z

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:96** by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) — 2025-02-21T12:11:18Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
```

  Do we want to have a field in status for the result of applying weights to `ConsumedResources` so it's easier to monitor and debug?

```diff
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution.

+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.

+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.

+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues.

+type FairSharing struct {

+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`

+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
```

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2025-02-24T10:55:55Z

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:152** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2025-02-24T10:55:55Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,237 @@
+# KEP-4136: Admission Fair Sharing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+
+This model has multiple assumptions:
+
+* Workloads can be preempted.
+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources. 
+
+However, these assumptions are not universal. Sometimes:
+
+* Workloads should not be preempted.
+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.
+* Fairness should not win over getting the workloads eventually completed.
+
+In that case the existing mode doesn’t work and a different one needs to be employed.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Establish a method for how shared resource usage is calculated and recorded and how users can fine tune the mechanism.
+* Allow to specify a fair admission scope at either individual Cluster Queue or Cohort scope.
+* Allow to specify the relative importance of LocalQueues targeting the same ClusterQueue.
+* Amend the admission mechanism to work on admission scopes instead of only on ClusterQueues. 
+* Select the appropriate admission candidates for each of the admission scopes and admit them according to the selected queueing policy.
+* Make the new mechanism complementary to the existing preemption-based fair sharing
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Store time series data inside K8S.
+* Provide precise shared resource usage accounting or billing.
+
+## Proposal
+
+* Modify CQ’s FairSharing struct with 
+
+type FairSharing struct {
+	// Weight denotes how important the given queue when competing against other queues 
+// for unused shared resources. The exact impact of the weight in fair share calculations
+// depends on the fair share algorithm used. Default = 1.
+	Weight *resource.Quantity `json:"weight,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Expand LQ spec with the same FairSharing struct (Cohort will be expanded with FairSharing 
+as a part of the Preemptive FS implementation in hierarchical structure).
+
+* Modify FairSharingStatus struct with 
+
+
+type FairSharingStatus struct {
+	// WeightShare represents the usage above nominal quota, with the weight applied in.
+	// The bigger the value is the more shared resources has been allocated and the less 
+	// entitled the queue is for more shared resources. 
+	// The exact details and the interpretation of the value depends on 
+    // the fair sharing algorithm used.
+	WeightedShare int64 `json:"weightedShare"`
+
+	
+	// ConsumedResources represents the aggregated usage of resources over time,
+	// with decaying function applied. 
+	// The value is populated if usage consumption functionality is enabled in Kueue config.
+	ConsumedResources map[string]resource.Quantity `json:"consumedResources,omitempty"`
+
+	// LastUpdate is the time when share and consumed resources were updated.
+	LastUpdate metav1.Time `json:"lastUpdate,omitempty"`
+}
+
+* Add FairSharingStatus to LocalQueue (and Cohort).
+
+* Create a new struct AdmissionScope and make it an optional field for CQ and Cohort Spec. If
+not provided, CQ or Cohort is not considered an AdmissionScope and is not a subject for new
+admission logic. If there are two AdmissionScopes on the path from CQ/Cohort to the top of
+the hierarchy tree, the higher one is used.
+
+Const (
+	// FairSharing based on usage, with QueuingStrategy as defined in CQ.
+	UsageBasedFairSharing AdmissionMode = UsageBasedFairSharing 
+
+NoFairSharing AdmissionMode = NoFairSharing	
+)
+
+type AdmissionScope struct {
+AdmissionMode AdmissionMode
+}
+
+* When selecting candidates for admission groups all workloads from LQ to CQ or the
+topmost Cohort that is marked with AdmissionScope. Then sort them using criterias:
+
+- Usage vector  built from ConsumedResources from TopCohort to LQ
+- Priority
+- Timestamp
+
+Let’s look at a couple scenarios:
+
+1. AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is FIFO, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. Kueue considers
+all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and fair sharing
+is applied to all workloads.
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. Other workloads are not attempted
+until the first one is not admitted.
+
+2.  AdmissionScope at CQ, CQ queueing policy is BestEffort, 3 LQ pointing to CQ. 
+Kueue considers all CQ resources and potentially borrowed resources as “shared” resources and
+fair sharing is applied to all workloads.
+
+Kueue sorts the workloads by their LQ usage (if mode is not NoFairSharing), priority and
+timestamp and tries to admit the first one from the list. If it fails and the second, third
+or following is possible then that workload is admitted, under condition that it might get preempted.
+
+3. AdmissionScope at Cohort level - Kueue operates in a mixed mode. Inside CQ workloads are
+selected according to their AdmissionMode (if specified). If a workload fits entirely into
+nominal quota, then it is admitted immediately, if not it goes into cohort-level fair sharing.
+For Cohort we select all the “sticking out” workloads, and sort them by their CQ usage, priority
```

  Updated/

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2025-02-24T11:04:46Z

- **keps/4136-admission-fair-sharing/README.md:147** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2025-02-24T11:04:46Z

```diff
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)

+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP describes the mechanism for fair admission of workloads coming from a group of
+different sources (like Cluster and Local Queues) based on the source shared resource usage.
+Workloads from sources that use less are admitted before workloads coming from sources that use more. 
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently Kueue has a Fair Sharing mechanism that enforces fair-sharing of unused resources
+via preemption. If one Cluster Queue is using much more of the resources than the other one
+that is in need, some workloads from the first one may be preempted to allow more “fair” distribution. 
+

+* Users get a proper quota to do their regular business.
+* Users come from multiple teams/organizations and they would rather have a strict policy but 
+fair policy than show understanding to those consuming all shared resources.

+* Users operate on a shared but bigger quota.

+
```
